	ama bâbat i to ni¬ya 	this is not worthy(vovoth|bâbat:bu¬bad) of you

	ba dang i barz : in a loud voice; [by Ton/Dong of Berg/bark(high:loud)]

	la kwe fer i kurdî bûy? where did you learn Kurdish?;
	ba feřo for free, for nothing, for no reason; 
 	bu na : to be almost, not to quite be  // BÛN بوون b-  BE +++ being @EG
 	aw bû ba pâshâ : he became king; 
  ... nabe niya : is nothing but ...
	
Circumflexed vowels follow uncircumflexed vowels in alphabetization. The furtive i is indicated by italicization, e.g. 
bâwik ‘father’ but bâwkî ‘his father.’  very remote!! --

Abbreviations: adj. = adjective; cond. = conditional; demon. = demonstrative; imprs. = impersonal (verb is always in the 3rd person singular); impt. = imperative; pl. = plural; pron. = pronoun; sing. = singular; subj. = subjunctive; pres. = present; v.i. = verb intransitive; v.p. = verb passive; v.t. = verb transitive (transitive implies that the past tense is formed on the ergative model, not that the verb necessarily takes a direct object either in Kurdish or in English).
Generally, compound verbs are listed under the nonverbal element of the com_pound; compounds with frequently-occurring elements like dâ-, hał-, and pe_are listed under the verb.
